function
google_ad_request_done(google_ads)
{




window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Eric_Clapton';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"eric,_,clapton,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Eric
Patrick
Clapton</b>,
<span
style="font-size:85%"><a
href="/wiki/Commander_of_The_Most_Excellent_Order_of_the_British_Empire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Commander
of
The
Most
Excellent
Order
of
the
British
Empire"
class="mw-redirect">CBE</a></span>,
(born
<span
class="nowrap">30
March</span>
1945)
is
an
English
musician,
singer
and
songwriter.
He
is
the
only
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_inductees?qsrc=3044#Multiple_inductees"
title="List
of
Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame
inductees">three-time
inductee</a>
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>:
once
as
a
solo
artist
and
separately
as
a
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Yardbirds">the
Yardbirds</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Cream_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cream
(band)">Cream</a>.
Clapton
has
been
referred
to
as
one
of
the
most
important
and
influential
guitarists
of
all
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-AST_1-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AST-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_guitarists_considered_the_greatest?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
guitarists
considered
the
greatest"
class="mw-redirect">ranked
second</a>
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone
(magazine)"
class="mw-redirect">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
magazine's
list
of
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Top_100_Greatest_Guitar_Players_of_all_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
100
Greatest
Guitar
Players
of
all
Time"
class="mw-redirect">100
Greatest
Guitarists
of
All
Time</a>&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-RS_2-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
fourth
in
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_Guitar_Corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
Guitar
Corporation">Gibson's</a>
&quot;Top
50
Guitarists
of
All
Time&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Gibson_3-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Gibson-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
mid-1960s,
Clapton
left
the
Yardbirds
to
play
<a
href="/wiki/Blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues">blues</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/John_Mayall_%26_the_Bluesbreakers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Mayall
&amp;
the
Bluesbreakers">John
Mayall
&amp;
the
Bluesbreakers</a>.
Immediately
after
leaving
Mayall,
Clapton
joined
<a
href="/wiki/Cream_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cream
(band)">Cream</a>,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Power_trio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Power
trio">power
trio</a>
with
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Ginger_Baker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ginger
Baker">Ginger
Baker</a>
and
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Jack_Bruce?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jack
Bruce">Jack
Bruce</a>
in
which
Clapton
played
sustained
blues
improvisations
and
&quot;arty,
blues-based
psychedelic
pop.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Rock_Hall_4-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rock_Hall-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
most
of
the
1970s,
Clapton's
output
bore
the
influence
of
the
mellow
style
of
<a
href="/wiki/JJ_Cale?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="JJ
Cale">JJ
Cale</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Reggae?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reggae">reggae</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Marley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Marley">Bob
Marley</a>.
His
version
of
Marley's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Shot_the_Sheriff?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Shot
the
Sheriff">I
Shot
the
Sheriff</a>&quot;
helped
reggae
reach
a
mass
market.<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
of
his
most
popular
recordings
were
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Layla?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Layla">Layla</a>&quot;,
recorded
by
<a
href="/wiki/Derek_and_the_Dominos?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Derek
and
the
Dominos">Derek
and
the
Dominos</a>,
another
band
he
formed,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robert
Johnson">Robert
Johnson</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cross_Road_Blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cross
Road
Blues">Crossroads</a>&quot;,
recorded
by
Cream.
Following
the
death
of
his
son
Conor
in
1991,
Clapton's
grief
was
expressed
in
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tears_in_Heaven?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tears
in
Heaven">Tears
in
Heaven</a>&quot;,
which
featured
in
his
<i><a
href="/wiki/Unplugged_(Eric_Clapton_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unplugged
(Eric
Clapton
album)">Unplugged</a></i>
album.</p>








<p>Clapton
has
been
the
recipient
of
17
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>,
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Awards">Brit
Award</a>
for
Outstanding
Contribution
to
Music.
In
2004,
he
was
awarded
a
<a
href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Order
of
the
British
Empire">CBE</a>
at
Buckingham
Palace
for
services
to
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Brits_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Brits-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1998,
Clapton,
a
recovering
alcoholic
and
<a
href="/wiki/Drug_addiction?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drug
addiction"
class="mw-redirect">drug
addict</a>,
founded
the
<a
href="/wiki/Crossroads_Centre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crossroads
Centre">Crossroads
Centre</a>
on
<a
href="/wiki/Antigua?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Antigua">Antigua</a>,
a
medical
facility
for
recovering
substance
abusers.<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

style="overflow:hidden;height:;">

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life">Early
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Eric
Patrick
Clapton
was
born
in
<a
href="/wiki/Ripley,_Surrey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ripley,
Surrey">Ripley,
Surrey</a>,
England,
the
son
of
16-year-old
Patricia
Molly
Clapton
(b.
<span
class="nowrap">7
January</span>
1929
d.
March
1999)
and
Edward
Walter
Fryer
(<span
class="nowrap">21
March</span>
1920
–
<span
class="nowrap">15
May</span>
1985),
a
25-year-old
soldier
from
<a
href="/wiki/Montreal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Montreal">Montreal</a>,
Quebec.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Fryer
shipped
off
to
war
prior
to
Clapton's
birth
and
then
returned
to
Canada.
Clapton
grew
up
with
his
grandmother,
Rose,
and
her
second
husband,
Jack
Clapp,
who
was
stepfather
to
Patricia
Clapton
and
her
brother
Adrian,
believing
they
were
his
parents
and
that
his
mother
was
actually
his
older
sister.
The
similarity
in
surnames
gave
rise
to
the
erroneous
belief
that
Clapton's
real
surname
is
Clapp
(Reginald
Cecil
Clapton
was
the
name
of
Rose's
first
husband,
Eric
Clapton's
maternal
grandfather).<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
Years
later,
his
mother
married
another
Canadian
soldier
and
moved
to
Germany,<sup
id="cite_ref-CND_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-CND-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
leaving
young
Eric
with
his
grandparents
in
<a
href="/wiki/Surrey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surrey">Surrey</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-GUI_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-GUI-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Clapton
received
an
acoustic
<a
href="/wiki/Hoyer_guitars?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hoyer
guitars">Hoyer
guitar</a>,
made
in
Germany,
for
his
thirteenth
birthday,
but
the
inexpensive
steel-stringed
instrument
was
difficult
to
play
and
he
briefly
lost
interest.<sup
id="cite_ref-GUI_13-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-GUI-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
years
later
Clapton
picked
it
up
again
and
started
playing
consistently.<sup
id="cite_ref-GUI_13-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-GUI-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
was
influenced
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Blues_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues
music"
class="mw-redirect">blues</a>
from
an
early
age,
and
practised
long
hours
to
learn
the
<a
href="/wiki/Chord_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chord
(music)">chords</a>
of
blues
music
by
playing
along
to
the
records.<sup
id="cite_ref-clap_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-clap-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
preserved
his
practice
sessions
using
his
portable
<a
href="/wiki/Grundig?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grundig">Grundig</a>
reel-to-reel
tape
recorder,
listening
to
them
over
and
over
until
he
felt
he'd
got
it
right.<sup
id="cite_ref-clap_14-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-clap-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-thomp_15-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-thomp-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1961,
after
leaving
<a
href="/wiki/Hollyfield_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hollyfield
School">Hollyfield
School</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Surbiton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surbiton">Surbiton</a>,
Clapton
studied
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Kingston_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kingston
University">Kingston
College
of
Art</a>
but
was
dismissed
at
the
end
of
the
academic
year
because
his
focus
remained
on
music
rather
than
art.
His
guitar
playing
was
so
advanced
that,
by
the
age
of
16,
he
was
getting
noticed.<sup
id="cite_ref-thomp_15-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-thomp-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
Around
this
time,
Clapton
began
<a
href="/wiki/Busking?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Busking"
class="mw-redirect">busking</a>
around
<a
href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Thames?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kingston
upon
Thames">Kingston</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Richmond,_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Richmond,
London">Richmond</a>,
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/West_End_of_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="West
End
of
London">West
End</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1962,
Clapton
started
performing
as
a
duo
with
fellow
blues
enthusiast
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Brock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Brock">David
Brock</a>
in
pubs
around
Surrey.<sup
id="cite_ref-thomp_15-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-thomp-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
he
was
seventeen
years
old,
Clapton
joined
his
first
band,
an
early
British
<a
href="/wiki/R%26B?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="R&amp;B"
class="mw-redirect">R&amp;B</a>
group,
the
Roosters,
whose
other
guitarist
was
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_McGuinness_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
McGuinness
(musician)">Tom
McGuinness</a>.
He
stayed
with
this
band
from
January
through
August
1963.<sup
id="cite_ref-BIOG_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BIOG-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
October
of
that
year,
Clapton
did
a
seven-<a
href="/wiki/Gig_(musical_performance)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gig
(musical
performance)"
class="mw-redirect">gig</a>
stint
with
<a
href="/wiki/Brian_Casser?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brian
Casser">Casey
Jones
&amp;
the
Engineers</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-BIOG_17-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BIOG-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_career.2C_breakthrough.2C_and_international_success">Early
career,
breakthrough,
and
international
success</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Early
career,
breakthrough,
and
international
success">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="The_Yardbirds_and_the_Bluesbreakers">The
Yardbirds
and
the
Bluesbreakers</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
The
Yardbirds
and
the
Bluesbreakers">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
articles:









<a
href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Yardbirds">The
Yardbirds</a>
and









<a
href="/wiki/John_Mayall_%26_the_Bluesbreakers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Mayall
&amp;
the
Bluesbreakers">John
Mayall
&amp;
the
Bluesbreakers</a>







</div>








<p>In
October
1963,
Clapton
joined
The
Yardbirds,
a
blues-influenced
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
roll">rock
and
roll</a>
band,
and
stayed
with
them
until
March
1965.
Synthesising
influences
from
<a
href="/wiki/Chicago_blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chicago
blues">Chicago
blues</a>
and
leading
blues
guitarists
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buddy
Guy">Buddy
Guy</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Freddie_King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Freddie
King">Freddie
King</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/B._B._King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B.
B.
King"
class="mw-redirect">B.
B.
King</a>,
Clapton
forged
a
distinctive
style
and
rapidly
became
one
of
the
most
talked-about
guitarists
in
the
British
music
scene.<sup
id="cite_ref-unuhsh_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unuhsh-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
initially
played
<a
href="/wiki/Chess_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chess
Records">Chess</a>/<a
href="/wiki/Checker_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Checker
Records">Checker</a>/<a
href="/wiki/Vee-Jay_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vee-Jay
Records">Vee-Jay</a>
blues
numbers
and
began
to
attract
a
large
<a
href="/wiki/Cult_following?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cult
following">cult
following</a>
when
they
took
over
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stones"
class="mw-redirect">Rolling
Stones</a>'
residency
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Crawdaddy_Club?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crawdaddy
Club">Crawdaddy
Club</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Richmond,_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Richmond,
London">Richmond</a>.
They
toured
England
with
American
bluesman
<a
href="/wiki/Sonny_Boy_Williamson_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sonny
Boy
Williamson
II">Sonny
Boy
Williamson
II</a>;
a
joint
LP
album,
recorded
in
December
1963,
was
issued
in
1965.</p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Royal_Albert_Hall,_London.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Royal_Albert_Hall%2C_London.jpg/220px-Royal_Albert_Hall%2C_London.jpg"
width="220"
height="142"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Royal_Albert_Hall%2C_London.jpg/330px-Royal_Albert_Hall%2C_London.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Royal_Albert_Hall%2C_London.jpg/440px-Royal_Albert_Hall%2C_London.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Royal_Albert_Hall,_London.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Since
appearing
at
the











<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Albert
Hall">Royal
Albert
Hall</a>
for
the
first
time
in
1964,
Clapton
has
performed
at
the
venue
almost
200
times.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>It
was
during
this
time
period
that
Clapton's
Yardbirds
rhythm
guitarist,
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Dreja?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Dreja">Chris
Dreja</a>,
recalled
that
whenever
Clapton
broke
a
guitar
string
during
a
concert,
he
would
stay
on
stage
and
replace
it.
The
English
audiences
would
wait
out
the
delay
by
doing
what
is
called
a
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Slow_clap?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slow
clap"
class="mw-redirect">slow
handclap</a>&quot;.
Clapton
told
his
official
biographer,
Ray
Coleman,
that,
&quot;My
nickname
of
'Slowhand'
came
from
<a
href="/wiki/Giorgio_Gomelsky?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Giorgio
Gomelsky">Giorgio
Gomelsky</a>.
He
coined
it
as
a
good
pun.
He
kept
saying
I
was
a
fast
player,
so
he
put
together
the
slow
handclap
phrase
into
Slowhand
as
a
play
on
words&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
December
1964,
Clapton
made
his
first
appearance
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Albert
Hall">Royal
Albert
Hall</a>,
London
with
The
Yardbirds.
Since
then,
Clapton
has
performed
at
the
Hall
almost
200
times,
and
has
stated
that
performing
at
the
venue
is
like
&quot;playing
in
my
front
room&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
March
1965
the
Yardbirds
had
their
first
major
hit,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/For_Your_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="For
Your
Love">For
Your
Love</a>&quot;,
on
which
Clapton
played
guitar.
The
Yardbirds
elected
to
move
toward
a
pop-oriented
sound,
in
part
because
of
the
success
of
&quot;For
Your
Love&quot;,
written
by
pop
songwriter-for-hire
<a
href="/wiki/Graham_Gouldman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Graham
Gouldman">Graham
Gouldman</a>
(who
would
achieve
success
as
a
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/10cc?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="10cc">10cc</a>),
who
had
also
written
hit
songs
for
<a
href="/wiki/Herman%27s_Hermits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Herman's
Hermits">Herman's
Hermits</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Hollies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Hollies">The
Hollies</a>.
Still
musically
devoted
to
the
blues,
Clapton
was
opposed
to
the
move,
and
left
the
band.
He
recommended
fellow
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmy
Page">Jimmy
Page</a>
as
his
replacement,
but
Page
declined
out
of
loyalty
to
Clapton,<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
putting
<a
href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jeff
Beck">Jeff
Beck</a>
forward.<sup
id="cite_ref-unuhsh_18-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unuhsh-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
While
Beck
and
Page
played
together
in
the
Yardbirds,
the
trio
of
Beck,
Page,
and
Clapton
were
never
in
the
group
together.
However,
the
trio
did
appear
on
the
12-date
benefit
tour
for
<i>Action
for
Research
into
<a
href="/wiki/Multiple_Sclerosis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Multiple
Sclerosis"
class="mw-redirect">Multiple
Sclerosis</a></i>
in
1983.</p>








<p>Clapton
joined
<a
href="/wiki/John_Mayall_%26_the_Bluesbreakers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Mayall
&amp;
the
Bluesbreakers">John
Mayall
&amp;
the
Bluesbreakers</a>
in
April
1965,
only
to
quit
a
few
months
later.
In
the
summer
of
1965
he
left
for
Greece
with
a
band
called
The
Glands,
which
included
his
old
friend
Ben
Palmer
on
piano.
In
November
1965
he
rejoined
John
Mayall.
During
his
second
Bluesbreakers
stint,
Clapton
gained
a
reputation
as
the
best
blues
guitarist
on
the
club
circuit.
Although
Clapton
gained
world
fame
for
his
playing
on
the
influential
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Blues_Breakers_with_Eric_Clapton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues
Breakers
with
Eric
Clapton">Blues
Breakers
–
John
Mayall
–
With
Eric
Clapton</a></i>,
this
album
was
not
released
until
he
had
left
the
band
for
the
last
time.
Having
swapped
his
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Telecaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Telecaster">Fender
Telecaster</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Vox_AC30?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vox
AC30">Vox
AC30</a>
amplifier
for
a
1960
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
Les
Paul">Gibson
Les
Paul
Standard</a>
guitar
and
<a
href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marshall
Amplification">Marshall
amplifier</a>,
Clapton's
sound
and
playing
inspired
a
well-publicised
<a
href="/wiki/Graffiti?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Graffiti">graffito</a>
that
<a
href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honorific
nicknames
in
popular
music">deified
him</a>
with
the
famous
<a
href="/wiki/Slogan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slogan">slogan</a>
&quot;Clapton
is
God&quot;.
The
phrase
was
spray-painted
by
an
admirer
on
a
wall
in
an
<a
href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Islington?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="London
Borough
of
Islington">Islington</a>
<a
href="/wiki/London_Underground?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="London
Underground">Underground</a>
station
in
the
autumn
of
1967.
The
graffiti
was
captured
in
a
now-famous
photograph,
in
which
a
dog
is
<a
href="/wiki/Urination?qsrc=3044#Canidae"
title="Urination">urinating
on
the
wall</a>.
Clapton
is
reported
to
have
been
embarrassed
by
the
slogan,
saying
in
his
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_South_Bank_Show?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
South
Bank
Show">The
South
Bank
Show</a></i>
profile
in
1987,
&quot;I
never
accepted
that
I
was
the
greatest
guitar
player
in
the
world.
I
always
<i>wanted</i>
to
be
the
greatest
guitar
player
in
the
world,
but
that's
an
ideal,
and
I
accept
it
as
an
ideal&quot;.
The
phrase
began
to
appear
in
other
areas
of
Islington
throughout
the
mid-1960s.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Cream">Cream</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Cream">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Cream_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cream
(band)">Cream
(band)</a>







</div>








<p>Clapton
left
the
Bluesbreakers
in
July
1966
(to
be
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Peter_Green_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Peter
Green
(musician)">Peter
Green</a>)
and
was
invited
by
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Ginger_Baker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ginger
Baker">Ginger
Baker</a>
to
play
in
his
newly
formed
band
Cream,
one
of
the
earliest
<a
href="/wiki/Supergroup_(bands)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Supergroup
(bands)"
class="mw-redirect">supergroups</a>,
with
<a
href="/wiki/Jack_Bruce?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jack
Bruce">Jack
Bruce</a>
on
bass
(previously
of
the
Bluesbreakers,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Graham_Bond?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Graham
Bond">Graham
Bond
Organisation</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Manfred_Mann?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Manfred
Mann">Manfred
Mann</a>).
Before
the
formation
of
Cream,
Clapton
was
not
well
known
in
the
United
States;
he
left
the
Yardbirds
before
&quot;For
Your
Love&quot;
hit
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100">American
Top
Ten</a>,
and
had
yet
to
perform
there.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
his
time
with
Cream,
Clapton
began
to
develop
as
a
singer,
songwriter,
and
guitarist,
though
Bruce
took
most
of
the
lead
vocals
and
wrote
the
majority
of
the
material
with
lyricist
<a
href="/wiki/Pete_Brown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pete
Brown">Pete
Brown</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-unuhsh_18-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unuhsh-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cream's
first
gig
was
an
unofficial
performance
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Twisted_Wheel_Club?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Twisted
Wheel
Club">Twisted
Wheel
Club</a>
in
Manchester
on
<span
class="nowrap">29
July</span>
1966
before
their
full
debut
two
nights
later
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/National_Jazz_and_Blues_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="National
Jazz
and
Blues
Festival">National
Jazz
and
Blues
Festival</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Windsor,_Berkshire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Windsor,
Berkshire">Windsor</a>.
Cream
established
its
enduring
legend
with
the
high-volume
blues
jamming
and
extended
solos
of
their
live
shows.</p>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">

/></a>

class="thumbcaption">











<div

Clapton
(right)
with
Cream









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>By
early
1967,
as
fans
of
the
emerging
blues-rock
sound
in
Britain
had
begun
to
portray
Clapton
as
Britain's
top
guitarist;
however,
he
found
himself
rivalled
by
the
emergence
of
<a
href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimi
Hendrix">Jimi
Hendrix</a>,
an
<a
href="/wiki/Acid_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Acid
rock">acid
rock</a>-infused
guitarist
who
used
wailing
<a
href="/wiki/Audio_feedback?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Audio
feedback">feedback</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Effects_unit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Effects
unit">effects
pedals</a>
to
create
new
sounds
for
the
instrument.
Hendrix
attended
a
performance
of
the
newly
formed
Cream
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/University_of_Westminster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="University
of
Westminster">Central
London
Polytechnic</a>
on
<span
class="nowrap">1
October</span>
1966,
during
which
Hendrix
sat
in
on
a
double-timed
version
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Killing_Floor_(Howlin%27_Wolf_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Killing
Floor
(Howlin'
Wolf
song)">Killing
Floor</a>&quot;.
Top
UK
stars,
including
Clapton,
<a
href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pete
Townshend">Pete
Townshend</a>,
and
members
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Rolling
Stones">The
Rolling
Stones</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>,
avidly
attended
Hendrix's
early
club
performances.
Hendrix's
arrival
had
an
immediate
and
major
effect
on
the
next
phase
of
Clapton's
career,
although
Clapton
continued
to
be
recognised
in
UK
music
polls
as
the
premier
guitarist.</p>








<p>Clapton
first
visited
the
United
States
while
touring
with
Cream.
In
March
1967,
Cream
performed
a
nine-show
stand
at
the
RKO
Theater
in
New
York.
They
recorded
<i><a
href="/wiki/Disraeli_Gears?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Disraeli
Gears">Disraeli
Gears</a></i>
in
New
York
from
<span
class="nowrap">11–15
May</span>
1967.
Cream's
repertoire
varied
from
hard
rock
(&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Feel_Free?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Feel
Free">I
Feel
Free</a>&quot;)
to
lengthy
blues-based
instrumental
jams
(&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Spoonful?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spoonful">Spoonful</a>&quot;).
<i>Disraeli
Gears</i>
featured
Clapton's
searing
guitar
lines,
Bruce's
soaring
vocals
and
prominent,
fluid
bass
playing,
and
Baker's
powerful,
polyrhythmic
jazz-influenced
drumming.
Together,
Cream's
talents
secured
them
as
an
influential
<a
href="/wiki/Power_trio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Power
trio">power
trio</a>.</p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:142px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Fool_guitar_(replica).jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg/140px-The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg"
width="140"
height="367"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg/210px-The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg/280px-The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Fool_guitar_(replica).jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Clapton's











<a
href="/wiki/The_Fool_(guitar)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Fool
(guitar)">The
Fool
guitar</a>











<i>(replica
shown)</i>,
with
its
bright
artwork
and
famous
&quot;woman
tone&quot;,
was
symbolic
of
the
1960s
psychedelic
rock
era.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
28
months,
Cream
had
become
a
commercial
success,
selling
millions
of
records
and
playing
throughout
the
U.S.
and
Europe.
They
redefined
the
instrumentalist's
role
in
rock
and
were
one
of
the
first
blues-rock
bands
to
emphasise
musical
virtuosity
and
lengthy
jazz-style
improvisation
sessions.
Their
U.S.
hit
singles
include
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Sunshine_of_Your_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sunshine
of
Your
Love">Sunshine
of
Your
Love</a>&quot;
(#5,
1968),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/White_Room?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="White
Room">White
Room</a>&quot;
(#6,
1968)
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Crossroads_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crossroads
(song)"
class="mw-redirect">Crossroads</a>&quot;
(#28,
1969)
–
a
live
version
of
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robert
Johnson
(musician)"
class="mw-redirect">Robert
Johnson</a>'s
&quot;Cross
Road
Blues&quot;.
Though
Cream
was
hailed
as
one
of
the
greatest
groups
of
its
day,
and
the
adulation
of
Clapton
as
a
guitar
legend
reached
new
heights,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Supergroup
(music)">supergroup</a>
was
short-lived.
Drug
and
alcohol
use
escalated
tension
between
the
three
members,
and
conflicts
between
Bruce
and
Baker
eventually
led
to
Cream's
demise.
A
strongly
critical
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
review
of
a
concert
of
the
group's
second
headlining
U.S.
tour
was
another
significant
factor
in
the
trio's
demise,
and
it
affected
Clapton
profoundly.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Cream's
farewell
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Goodbye_(Cream_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Goodbye
(Cream
album)">Goodbye</a></i>,
featuring
live
performances
recorded
at
<a
href="/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood,_California)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Forum
(Inglewood,
California)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Forum</a>,
Los
Angeles,
<span
class="nowrap">19
October</span>
1968,
was
released
shortly
after
Cream
disbanded;
it
also
featured
the
studio
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Badge_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Badge
(song)">Badge</a>&quot;,
co-written
by
Clapton
and
<a
href="/wiki/George_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Harrison">George
Harrison</a>.
Clapton
met
Harrison
and
became
friends
with
him
after
the
Beatles
shared
a
bill
with
the
Clapton-era
Yardbirds
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/London_Palladium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="London
Palladium">London
Palladium</a>.
The
close
friendship
between
Clapton
and
Harrison
resulted
in
Clapton
playing
on
Harrison's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps">While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps</a>&quot;
from
the
Beatles'
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles
(album)">White
Album</a></i>
(1968).
Harrison
also
released
his
solo
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wonderwall_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wonderwall
Music">Wonderwall
Music</a></i>,
in
1968.
It
became
the
first
of
many
Harrison
solo
records
to
feature
Clapton
on
guitar.
Clapton
would
go
largely
uncredited
for
his
contributions
to
Harrison's
albums
due
to
contractual
restraints.
The
pair
would
often
play
live
together
as
each
other's
guest.
A
year
after
Harrison's
death
in
2001,
Clapton
helped
organise
a
<a
href="/wiki/Concert_for_George?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concert
for
George">tribute
concert</a>,
for
which
he
was
musical
director.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1969,
when
The
Beatles
were
recording/filming
what
became
<i><a
href="/wiki/Let_It_Be_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
It
Be
(film)">Let
It
Be</a></i>,
tensions
became
so
acute
that
Harrison
quit
the
group
for
several
days,
prompting
the
others
to
consider
replacing
him
with
Clapton,
an
idea
that
particularly
appealed
to
<a
href="/wiki/John_Lennon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Lennon">John
Lennon</a>,
who
was
captured
on
tape
saying
that
if:
&quot;George
doesn’t
come
back
by
Monday
or
Tuesday,
we
ask
Eric
Clapton
to
play&quot;,
and
that
this
would
be
congenial
to
Clapton
in
that
The
Beatles,
unlike
Cream,
&quot;would
give
him
full
scope
to
play
his
guitar&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-wheres_eric_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wheres_eric-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
Years
later,
Clapton
commented
on
the
absurdity
of
this
idea:
&quot;There
may
have
been
[a
suggestion
that
I
would
be
asked
to
join
The
Beatles
in
January
1969].
The
problem
with
that
was
I
had
bonded
or
was
developing
a
relationship
with
George,
exclusive
of
them.
I
think
it
fitted
a
need
of
his
and
mine,
that
he
could
elevate
himself
by
having
this
guy
that
could
be
like
a
gunslinger
to
them.
Lennon
would
use
my
name
every
now
and
then
for
clout,
as
if
I
was
the
fastest
gun.
So,
I
don’t
think
I
could
have
been
brought
into
the
whole
thing
because
I
was
too
much
a
mate
of
George’s&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-wheres_eric_27-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wheres_eric-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Cream
briefly
reunited
in
1993
to
perform
at
the
ceremony
inducting
them
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>;
a
full
reunion
took
place
in
May
2005,
with
Clapton,
Bruce,
and
Baker
playing
four
sold-out
concerts
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Albert
Hall">Royal
Albert
Hall</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
three
shows
at
New
York's
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>
that
October.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
Recordings
from
the
London
shows,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall_London_May_2-3-5-6,_2005?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Albert
Hall
London
May
2-3-5-6,
2005">Royal
Albert
Hall
London
May
2-3-5-6,
2005</a></i>,
were
released
on
CD,
LP,
and
DVD
in
September/December
2005.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Blind_Faith.2C_and_Delaney_and_Bonnie_and_Friends">Blind
Faith,
and
Delaney
and
Bonnie
and
Friends</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
Blind
Faith,
and
Delaney
and
Bonnie
and
Friends">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
articles:









<a
href="/wiki/Blind_Faith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blind
Faith">Blind
Faith</a>
and









<a
href="/wiki/Delaney_and_Bonnie_and_Friends?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delaney
and
Bonnie
and
Friends"
class="mw-redirect">Delaney
and
Bonnie
and
Friends</a>







</div>








<p>Clapton's
next
group,
<a
href="/wiki/Blind_Faith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blind
Faith">Blind
Faith</a>
(1969),
was
composed
of
Cream
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Ginger_Baker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ginger
Baker">Ginger
Baker</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Winwood">Steve
Winwood</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Traffic_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Traffic
(band)">Traffic</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ric_Grech?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ric
Grech">Ric
Grech</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Family_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Family
(band)">Family</a>,
and
yielded
one
LP
and
one
arena-circuit
tour.
The
supergroup
debuted
before
100,000
fans
in
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyde
Park,
London">Hyde
Park</a>
on
<span
class="nowrap">7
June</span>
1969.
They
performed
several
dates
in
Scandinavia
and
began
a
sold-out
American
tour
in
July
before
their
only
album
was
released.
The
LP
<i><a
href="/wiki/Blind_Faith_(Blind_Faith_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blind
Faith
(Blind
Faith
album)">Blind
Faith</a></i>
consisted
of
just
six
songs,
one
of
them
a
15-minute
jam
entitled
&quot;Do
What
You
Like&quot;.
The
album's
jacket
image
of
a
topless
pubescent
girl
was
deemed
controversial
in
the
United
States
and
was
replaced
by
a
photograph
of
the
band.
Blind
Faith
dissolved
after
less
than
seven
months.</p>








<p>Clapton
subsequently
toured
as
a
sideman
for
an
act
that
had
opened
for
Blind
Faith,
<a
href="/wiki/Delaney_and_Bonnie_and_Friends?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delaney
and
Bonnie
and
Friends"
class="mw-redirect">Delaney
and
Bonnie
and
Friends</a>.
He
also
played
two
dates
as
a
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Plastic_Ono_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Plastic
Ono
Band"
class="mw-redirect">The
Plastic
Ono
Band</a>
that
autumn,
including
a
recorded
performance
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Toronto_Rock_and_Roll_Revival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toronto
Rock
and
Roll
Revival">Toronto
Rock
and
Roll
Revival</a>
in
September
1969
released
as
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_Peace_in_Toronto_1969?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
Peace
in
Toronto
1969">Live
Peace
in
Toronto
1969</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-lenn_31-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lenn-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
30
September
1969,
Clapton
played
lead
guitar
on
Lennon's
second
solo
single,
<a
href="/wiki/Cold_Turkey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cold
Turkey">Cold
Turkey</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
15
December
1969
Clapton
performed
with
<a
href="/wiki/John_Lennon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Lennon">John
Lennon</a>,
George
Harrison,
and
others
as
the
Plastic
Ono
Band
at
a
fundraiser
for
<a
href="/wiki/UNICEF?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>
in
London.<sup
id="cite_ref-lenn_31-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lenn-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Delaney_Bramlett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delaney
Bramlett">Delaney
Bramlett</a>
encouraged
Clapton
in
his
singing
and
writing.
During
the
summer
of
1969,
Clapton
and
Bramlett
contributed
to
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Music_From_Free_Creek?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
From
Free
Creek"
class="mw-redirect">Music
From
Free
Creek</a></i>
&quot;supersession&quot;
project.
Clapton,
appearing
as
&quot;King
Cool&quot;
for
contractual
reasons,
played
with
<a
href="/wiki/Dr._John?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dr.
John">Dr.
John</a>
on
three
songs,
joined
by
Bramlett
on
two
tracks.</p>








<p>Using
the
Bramletts'
backing
group
and
an
all-star
cast
of
session
players
(including
<a
href="/wiki/Leon_Russell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leon
Russell">Leon
Russell</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Stills">Stephen
Stills</a>),
Clapton
recorded
his
first
solo
album
during
two
brief
tour
hiatuses,
fittingly
named
<i><a
href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Clapton
(album)">Eric
Clapton</a></i>.
Delaney
Bramlett
co-wrote
six
of
the
songs
with
Clapton,<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bonnie_Bramlett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bonnie
Bramlett">Bonnie
Bramlett</a>
co-wrote
&quot;Let
It
Rain&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
yielded
the
unexpected
U.S.
No.&nbsp;18
hit,
<a
href="/wiki/J._J._Cale?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="J.
J.
Cale"
class="mw-redirect">J.
J.
Cale</a>'s
&quot;After
Midnight&quot;.
Clapton
went
with
Delaney
and
Bonnie
from
the
stage
to
the
studio
with
the
Dominos
to
record
George
Harrison's
<i><a
href="/wiki/All_Things_Must_Pass?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
Things
Must
Pass">All
Things
Must
Pass</a></i>
in
spring
1970.
During
this
busy
period,
Clapton
also
recorded
with
other
artists
including
Dr.
John,
<a
href="/wiki/Leon_Russell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leon
Russell">Leon
Russell</a>,
Plastic
Ono
Band,
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Preston?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Preston">Billy
Preston</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Stills">Stephen
Stills</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ringo
Starr">Ringo
Starr</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Mason?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Mason">Dave
Mason</a>.</p>








<p>Other
notable
recordings
from
this
period
include
Clapton's
guitar
work
on
&quot;Go
Back
Home&quot;
from
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Stills">Stephen
Stills</a>'
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Stills
(album)">self-titled
first
solo
album</a>.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id=".22Layla.22_and_solo_career">&quot;Layla&quot;
and
solo
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a

and

career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"

and
the
Dominos</span>
<span

<p>With
the
intention
of
counteracting
the
&quot;star&quot;
cult
faction
that
had
begun
to
form
around
him,
Clapton
assembled
a
new
band
composed
of
Delaney
and
Bonnie's
former
<a
href="/wiki/Rhythm_section?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rhythm
section">rhythm
section</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Bobby_Whitlock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bobby
Whitlock">Bobby
Whitlock</a>
as
keyboardist
and
vocalist,
<a
href="/wiki/Carl_Radle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carl
Radle">Carl
Radle</a>
as
the
bassist,
and
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Jim_Gordon_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jim
Gordon
(musician)">Jim
Gordon</a>,
with
Clapton
playing
guitar.
It
was
his
intention
to
show
that
he
need
not
fill
a
starring
role,
and
functioned
well
as
a
member
of
an
ensemble.<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
this
period,
Clapton
was
increasingly
influenced
by
<a
href="/wiki/The_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Band">The
Band</a>
and
their
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Music_from_Big_Pink?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
from
Big
Pink">Music
from
Big
Pink</a></i>,
saying,
&quot;What
I
appreciated
about
The
Band
was
that
they
were
more
concerned
with
songs
and
singing.
They
would
have
three-
and
four-part
harmonies,
and
the
guitar
was
put
back
into
perspective
as
being
accompaniment.
That
suited
me
well,
because
I
had
gotten
so
tired
of
the
virtuosity—or
<i>pseudo</i>-virtuosity—thing
of
long,
boring
guitar
solos
just
because
they
were
expected.
The
Band
brought
things
back
into
perspective.
The
priority
was
the
song.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Derek_and_the_Dominos.png"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Derek_and_the_Dominos.png/220px-Derek_and_the_Dominos.png"
width="220"
height="163"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Derek_and_the_Dominos.png/330px-Derek_and_the_Dominos.png
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Derek_and_the_Dominos.png/440px-Derek_and_the_Dominos.png
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Derek_and_the_Dominos.png"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Clapton
(right)
with
Derek
and
the
Dominos









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>The
band
was
originally
called
&quot;Eric
Clapton
and
Friends&quot;.
The
name
&quot;Derek
and
the
Dominos&quot;
was
a
fluke
that
occurred
when
the
band's
provisional
name
of
&quot;Del
and
the
Dynamos&quot;
was
misread
as
Derek
and
the
Dominos.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton's
biography
states
that
Tony
Ashton
of
<a
href="/wiki/Ashton,_Gardner_and_Dyke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ashton,
Gardner
and
Dyke">Ashton,
Gardner
and
Dyke</a>
told
Clapton
to
call
the
band
&quot;Del
and
the
Dominos&quot;,
since
&quot;Del&quot;
was
his
nickname
for
Eric
Clapton.
Del
and
Eric
were
combined
and
the
final
name
became
&quot;Derek
and
the
Dominos&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-nxfddy_38-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nxfddy-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Clapton's
close
friendship
with
George
Harrison
brought
him
into
contact
with
Harrison's
wife,
<a
href="/wiki/Pattie_Boyd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pattie
Boyd">Pattie
Boyd</a>,
with
whom
he
became
deeply
infatuated.
When
she
spurned
his
advances,
Clapton's
unrequited
affections
prompted
most
of
the
material
for
the
Dominos'
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Layla
and
Other
Assorted
Love
Songs">Layla
and
Other
Assorted
Love
Songs</a></i>
(1970).
Heavily
blues-influenced,
the
album
features
the
twin
lead
guitars
of
Duane
Allman
and
Clapton,
with
Allman's
<a
href="/wiki/Slide_guitar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slide
guitar">slide
guitar</a>
as
a
key
ingredient
of
the
sound.
Working
at
<a
href="/wiki/Criteria_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Criteria
Studios">Criteria
Studios</a>
in
Miami
with
<a
href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Atlantic
Records">Atlantic
Records</a>
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Dowd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Dowd">Tom
Dowd</a>,
who
had
worked
with
Clapton
on
Cream's
<i>Disraeli
Gears</i>,
the
band
recorded
a
double
album.</p>








<p>The
album
features
the
hit
love
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Layla?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Layla">Layla</a>&quot;,
inspired
by
the
classical
poet
of
<a
href="/wiki/Persian_literature?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Persian
literature">Persian
literature</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nizami_Ganjavi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nizami
Ganjavi">Nizami
Ganjavi</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Layla_and_Majnun?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Layla
and
Majnun">The
Story
of
Layla
and
Majnun</a></i>,
a
copy
of
which
<a
href="/wiki/Ian_Dallas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ian
Dallas"
class="mw-redirect">Ian
Dallas</a>
had
given
to
Clapton.
The
book
moved
Clapton
profoundly,
as
it
was
the
tale
of
a
young
man
who
fell
hopelessly
in
love
with
a
beautiful,
unavailable
woman
and
who
went
crazy
because
he
could
not
marry
her.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
two
parts
of
&quot;Layla&quot;
were
recorded
in
separate
sessions:
the
opening
guitar
section
was
recorded
first,
and
for
the
second
section,
laid
down
several
months
later,
drummer
Jim
Gordon
played
the
piano
part
for
the
melody
which
he
claimed
to
write
(though
Bobby
Whitlock
claimed
that
Rita
Coolidge
wrote
it).<sup
id="cite_ref-nxfddy_38-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nxfddy-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
<i>Layla</i>
LP
was
actually
recorded
by
a
five-piece
version
of
the
group,
thanks
to
the
unforeseen
inclusion
of
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Duane_Allman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Duane
Allman">Duane
Allman</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Allman_Brothers_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Allman
Brothers
Band">The
Allman
Brothers
Band</a>.
A
few
days
into
the
Layla
sessions,
Dowd—who
was
also
producing
the
Allmans—invited
Clapton
to
an
Allman
Brothers
outdoor
concert
in
Miami.
The
two
guitarists
met
first
on
stage,
then
played
all
night
in
the
studio,
and
became
friends.
Duane
first
added
his
<a
href="/wiki/Slide_guitar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slide
guitar">slide
guitar</a>
to
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tell_the_Truth_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tell
the
Truth
(song)">Tell
the
Truth</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Nobody_Knows_You_When_You%27re_Down_and_Out?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nobody
Knows
You
When
You're
Down
and
Out">Nobody
Knows
You
When
You're
Down
and
Out</a>&quot;.
In
four
days,
the
five-piece
Dominos
recorded
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Key_to_the_Highway?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Key
to
the
Highway">Key
to
the
Highway</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Have_You_Ever_Loved_a_Woman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Have
You
Ever
Loved
a
Woman">Have
You
Ever
Loved
a
Woman</a>&quot;
(a
<a
href="/wiki/Blues_standard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues
standard"
class="mw-redirect">blues
standard</a>
popularised
by
<a
href="/wiki/Freddie_King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Freddie
King">Freddie
King</a>
and
others),
and
&quot;Why
Does
Love
Got
to
be
So
Sad&quot;.
In
September,
Duane
briefly
left
the
sessions
for
gigs
with
his
own
band,
and
the
four-piece
Dominos
recorded
&quot;I
Looked
Away&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bell_Bottom_Blues_(Derek_and_the_Dominos_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bell
Bottom
Blues
(Derek
and
the
Dominos
song)">Bell
Bottom
Blues</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;Keep
on
Growing&quot;.
Duane
returned
to
record
&quot;I
am
Yours&quot;,
&quot;Anyday&quot;,
and
&quot;It's
Too
Late&quot;.
On
9
September,
they
recorded
Hendrix's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Little_Wing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Little
Wing">Little
Wing</a>&quot;
and
the
title
track.
The
following
day,
the
final
track,
&quot;It's
Too
Late&quot;,
was
recorded.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">

2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a

target="_blank"

</div>
Eric
Clapton
in











<a
href="/wiki/Barcelona?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>,
1974









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Tragedy
dogged
the
group
throughout
its
brief
career.
During
the
sessions,
Clapton
was
devastated
by
news
of
the
death
of
Jimi
Hendrix;
eight
days
previously
the
band
had
cut
a
cover
of
&quot;Little
Wing&quot;
as
a
tribute
to
Hendrix.
On
<span
class="nowrap">17
September</span>
1970,
one
day
before
Hendrix's
death,
Clapton
had
purchased
a
<a
href="/wiki/Left-handedness?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Left-handedness"
class="mw-redirect">left-handed</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Stratocaster">Fender
Stratocaster</a>
that
he
had
planned
to
give
to
Hendrix
as
a
birthday
gift.
Adding
to
Clapton's
woes,
the
<i>Layla</i>
album
received
only
lukewarm
reviews
upon
release.
The
shaken
group
undertook
a
U.S.
tour
without
Allman,
who
had
returned
to
the
Allman
Brothers
Band.
Despite
Clapton's
later
admission
that
the
tour
took
place
amidst
a
veritable
blizzard
of
drugs
and
alcohol,
it
resulted
in
the
live
double
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/In_Concert_(Derek_and_the_Dominos_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Concert
(Derek
and
the
Dominos
album)">In
Concert</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
had
recorded
several
tracks
for
a
second
album
in
London
during
the
spring
of
1971
(five
of
which
were
released
on
the
Eric
Clapton
box-set
<i>Crossroads</i>),
but
the
results
were
mediocre.</p>








<p>A
second
record
was
in
the
works
when
a
clashing
of
egos
took
place
and
Clapton
walked,
thus
disbanding
the
group.
Allman
was
killed
in
a
motorcycle
accident
on
<span
class="nowrap">29
October</span>
1971.
Clapton
wrote
later
in
his
autobiography
that
he
and
Allman
were
inseparable
during
the
sessions
in
Florida;
he
talked
about
Allman
as
the
&quot;musical
brother
I'd
never
had
but
wished
I
did.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
Although
Radle
would
remain
Clapton's
bass
player
until
the
summer
of
1979
(Radle
died
in
May
1980
from
the
effects
of
alcohol
and
narcotics),
it
would
be
2003
before
Clapton
and
Whitlock
appeared
together
again
(Clapton
guested
on
Whitlock's
appearance
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Later_with_Jools_Holland?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Later
with
Jools
Holland"
class="mw-redirect">Later
with
Jools
Holland</a></i>
show).
Another
tragic
footnote
to
the
Dominos
story
was
the
fate
of
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Jim_Gordon_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jim
Gordon
(musician)">Jim
Gordon</a>,
who
was
an
undiagnosed
<a
href="/wiki/Schizophrenia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenic</a>
and
years
later
murdered
his
mother
during
a
<a
href="/wiki/Psychosis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Psychosis">psychotic
episode</a>.
Gordon
was
confined
to
16-years-to-life
imprisonment,
later
being
moved
to
a
mental
institution,
where
he
remains
today.<sup
id="cite_ref-unuhsh_18-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unuhsh-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Personal_challenges_and_early_solo_success">Personal
challenges
and
early
solo
success</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Personal
challenges
and
early
solo
success">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Clapton's
career
successes
in
the
1970s
were
in
stark
contrast
with
the
struggles
he
coped
with
in
his
personal
life,
which
was
troubled
by
romantic
longings
and
drug
and
alcohol
addiction.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
became
infatuated
with
Pattie
Boyd,
who
at
the
time
was
married
to
close
friend
<a
href="/wiki/George_Harrison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Harrison">George
Harrison</a>,
he
withdrew
from
recording
and
touring
as
the
band
broke
up
to
isolation
in
his
Surrey,
England,
residence.
There
he
nursed
a
<a
href="/wiki/Substance_abuse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Substance
abuse">heroin
addiction</a>,
which
resulted
in
a
lengthy
career
hiatus
interrupted
only
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Concert_for_Bangladesh?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concert
for
Bangladesh"
class="mw-redirect">Concert
for
Bangladesh</a>
in
August
1971
(where
he
passed
out
on
stage,
was
revived,
and
managed
to
finish
his
performance).<sup
id="cite_ref-unuhsh_18-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-unuhsh-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
January
1973,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Who?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Who">The
Who</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pete
Townshend">Pete
Townshend</a>
organised
a
comeback
concert
for
Clapton
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Rainbow_Theatre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rainbow
Theatre">Rainbow
Theatre</a>,
aptly
titled
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton%27s_Rainbow_Concert?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Clapton's
Rainbow
Concert">Rainbow
Concert</a>&quot;,
to
help
Clapton
kick
his
addiction.
Clapton
would
return
the
favour
by
playing
'The
Preacher'
in
<a
href="/wiki/Tommy_(1975_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tommy
(1975
film)">Ken
Russell's
film
version</a>
of
The
Who's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Tommy_(rock_opera)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tommy
(rock
opera)"
class="mw-redirect">Tommy</a></i>
in
1975;
his
appearance
in
the
film
(performing
&quot;Eyesight
to
the
Blind&quot;)
is
notable
as
he
is
clearly
wearing
a
fake
beard
in
some
shots,
the
result
of
deciding
to
shave
off
his
real
beard
after
the
initial
takes
in
an
attempt
to
force
the
director
to
remove
his
earlier
scene
from
the
movie
and
leave
the
set.<sup
id="cite_ref-nxfddy_38-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nxfddy-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg/220px-Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg"

class="thumbimage"

http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg/440px-Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg
