/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>











<a
href="/wiki/Yvonne_Elliman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yvonne
Elliman">Yvonne
Elliman</a>
with
Clapton
promoting











<i><a
href="/wiki/461_Ocean_Boulevard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="461
Ocean
Boulevard">461
Ocean
Boulevard</a></i>
in
1975









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
1974,
Clapton
was
partnered
with
Pattie
Boyd
(they
would
not
actually
marry
until
1979)
and
no
longer
using
heroin
(although
he
gradually
began
to
drink
heavily).
He
assembled
a
low-key
touring
band
that
included
Radle,
Miami
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/George_Terry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Terry">George
Terry</a>,
keyboardist
Dick
Sims
(who
died
in
2011<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>),
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Jamie_Oldaker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jamie
Oldaker">Jamie
Oldaker</a>,
and
vocalists
<a
href="/wiki/Yvonne_Elliman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yvonne
Elliman">Yvonne
Elliman</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Marcy_Levy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marcy
Levy"
class="mw-redirect">Marcy
Levy</a>
(also
known
as
Marcella
Detroit).
With
this
band
Clapton
recorded
<i><a
href="/wiki/461_Ocean_Boulevard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="461
Ocean
Boulevard">461
Ocean
Boulevard</a></i>
(1974),
an
album
with
an
emphasis
on
more
compact
songs
and
fewer
guitar
solos;
the
cover
version
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Shot_The_Sheriff?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Shot
The
Sheriff"
class="mw-redirect">I
Shot
The
Sheriff</a>&quot;
was
Clapton's
first
No.&nbsp;1
hit
and
was
important
in
bringing
<a
href="/wiki/Reggae?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reggae">reggae</a>
and
the
music
of
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Marley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Marley">Bob
Marley</a>
to
a
wider
audience.
The
1975
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/There%27s_One_in_Every_Crowd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="There's
One
in
Every
Crowd">There's
One
in
Every
Crowd</a></i>
continued
this
trend.
The
album's
original
title,
<i>The
World's
Greatest
Guitar
Player
(There's
One
in
Every
Crowd)</i>,
was
changed
before
pressing,
as
it
was
felt
its
ironic
intention
would
be
misunderstood.
The
band
toured
the
world
and
subsequently
released
the
1975
live
LP,
<i><a
href="/wiki/E.C._Was_Here?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="E.C.
Was
Here"
class="mw-redirect">E.C.
Was
Here</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
continued
to
release
albums
and
toured
regularly.
Highlights
of
the
period
include
<i><a
href="/wiki/No_Reason_to_Cry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="No
Reason
to
Cry">No
Reason
to
Cry</a></i>
(a
collaboration
with
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Dylan">Bob
Dylan</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Band">The
Band</a>);
<i><a
href="/wiki/Slowhand?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slowhand">Slowhand</a></i>,
which
featured
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wonderful_Tonight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wonderful
Tonight">Wonderful
Tonight</a>
and
a
second
JJ
Cale
cover,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cocaine_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cocaine
(song)">Cocaine</a>&quot;.
In
1976
he
performed,
alongside
a
string
of
notable
guests,
to
pay
tribute
to
the
farewell
performance
of
The
Band,
filmed
in
a
<a
href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Martin
Scorsese">Martin
Scorsese</a>
documentary
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Last_Waltz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Last
Waltz">The
Last
Waltz</a></i>.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Continued_success">Continued
success</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Continued
success">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>In
1981
Clapton
was
invited
by
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Martin_Lewis_(humorist)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Martin
Lewis
(humorist)">Martin
Lewis</a>
to
appear
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Amnesty_International?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Amnesty
International">Amnesty
International</a>
benefit
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Secret_Policeman%27s_Other_Ball?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Secret
Policeman's
Other
Ball">The
Secret
Policeman's
Other
Ball</a></i>.
Clapton
accepted
the
invitation
and
teamed
up
with
Jeff
Beck
to
perform
a
series
of
duets—reportedly
their
first-ever
billed
stage
collaboration.
Three
of
the
performances
were
released
on
the
album
of
the
show,
and
one
of
the
songs
was
featured
in
the
film.
The
performances
heralded
a
return
to
form
and
prominence
for
Clapton
in
the
new
decade.
Many
factors
had
influenced
Clapton's
comeback,
including
his
&quot;deepening
commitment
to
Christianity&quot;,
to
which
he
had
converted
prior
to
his
heroin
addiction.<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-amg_49-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-amg-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
an
embarrassing
fishing
incident,
Clapton
finally
called
his
manager
and
admitted
he
was
an
alcoholic.
In
January
1982
Roger
and
Clapton
flew
to
<a
href="/wiki/Minneapolis_%E2%80%93_St._Paul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Minneapolis
–
St.
Paul"
class="mw-redirect">Minneapolis
–
St.
Paul</a>;
Clapton
would
be
checked
in
at
<a
href="/wiki/Hazelden_Foundation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hazelden
Foundation">Hazelden
Treatment
Center</a>,
located
in
<a
href="/wiki/Center_City,_Minnesota?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Center
City,
Minnesota">Center
City,
Minnesota</a>.
On
the
flight
over,
Clapton
indulged
in
a
large
number
of
drinks,
for
fear
he
would
never
be
able
to
drink
again.
Clapton
is
quoted
as
saying
from
his
autobiography,
&quot;In
the
lowest
moments
of
my
life,
the
only
reason
I
didn't
commit
suicide
was
that
I
knew
I
wouldn't
be
able
to
drink
any
more
if
I
was
dead.
It
was
the
only
thing
I
thought
was
worth
living
for,
and
the
idea
that
people
were
about
to
try
and
remove
me
from
alcohol
was
so
terrible
that
I
drank
and
drank
and
drank,
and
they
had
to
practically
carry
me
into
the
clinic.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="thumb
tright">

at











<a

Arena</a>,











<span

</div>

<p>After
being
discharged,
it
was
recommended
by
doctors
of
Hazelden
that
Clapton
not
partake
in
any
activities
that
would
act
as
triggers
for
his
alcoholism
or
stress,
until
he
was
fully
situated
back
at
Hurtwood.
A
few
months
after
his
discharge,
Clapton
began
working
on
his
next
album,
against
the
Hazelden
doctors'
orders.
Working
with
Tom
Dowd,
Clapton
produced
what
he
thought
as
his
&quot;most
forced&quot;
album
to
date,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Money_and_Cigarettes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Money
and
Cigarettes">Money
and
Cigarettes</a></i>.</p>








<p>In
1984
he
performed
on
<a
href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pink
Floyd">Pink
Floyd</a>
member
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Waters?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Waters">Roger
Waters</a>'
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Pros_and_Cons_of_Hitch_Hiking?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Pros
and
Cons
of
Hitch
Hiking">The
Pros
and
Cons
of
Hitch
Hiking</a></i>,
and
went
on
tour
with
Waters
following
the
release
of
the
album.
Since
then
Waters
and
Clapton
have
had
a
close
relationship.
In
2005
they
performed
together
for
the
Tsunami
Relief
Fund.
In
2006
they
performed
at
the
Highclere
Castle,
in
aid
of
the
Countryside
Alliance,
playing
two
set
pieces
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wish_You_Were_Here_(Pink_Floyd_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wish
You
Were
Here
(Pink
Floyd
song)">Wish
You
Were
Here</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Comfortably_Numb?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Comfortably
Numb">Comfortably
Numb</a>&quot;.
Clapton,
now
a
seasoned
charity
performer,
played
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Live_Aid?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
Aid">Live
Aid</a>
concert
on
13
July
1985.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
offered
a
slot
close
to
peak
viewing
hours,
he
was
apparently
flattered.
As
Clapton
recovered
from
his
addictions,
his
album
output
continued
in
the
1980s,
including
two
produced
with
<a
href="/wiki/Phil_Collins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phil
Collins">Phil
Collins</a>,
1985's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Behind_the_Sun_(Eric_Clapton_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Behind
the
Sun
(Eric
Clapton
album)">Behind
the
Sun</a></i>,
which
produced
the
hits
&quot;Forever
Man&quot;
and
&quot;She's
Waiting&quot;,
and
1986's
<i><a
href="/wiki/August_(Eric_Clapton_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="August
(Eric
Clapton
album)">August</a></i>.</p>

class="thumb

<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

Concert,











<a

<p><i>August</i>
was
suffused
with
Collins's
trademark
drum
and
horn
sound,
and
became
Clapton's
biggest
seller
in
the
UK
to
date,
matching
his
highest
chart
position,
number
3.
The
album's
first
track,
the
hit
&quot;It's
in
the
Way
That
You
Use
It&quot;,
was
featured
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Cruise?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Cruise">Tom
Cruise</a>
–
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_Newman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
Newman">Paul
Newman</a>
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Color_of_Money?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Color
of
Money">The
Color
of
Money</a>.</i>
The
horn-peppered
&quot;Run&quot;
echoed
Collins'
&quot;Sussudio&quot;
and
rest
of
the
producer's
Genesis/solo
output,
while
&quot;Tearing
Us
Apart&quot;
(with
<a
href="/wiki/Tina_Turner?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tina
Turner">Tina
Turner</a>)
and
the
unimpressed
&quot;Miss
You&quot;
echoed
Clapton's
angry
sound.
This
rebound
kicked
off
Clapton's
two-year
period
of
touring
with
Collins
and
their
<i>August</i>
collaborates,
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Nathan_East?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nathan
East">Nathan
East</a>
and
keyboard
player/songwriter
Greg
Phillinganes.
While
on
tour
for
<i>August</i>,
two
concert
videos
were
recorded
of
the
four-man
band,
<i>Eric
Clapton
Live
from
Montreux</i>
and
<i>Eric
Clapton
and
Friends</i>.
Clapton
later
remade
&quot;After
Midnight&quot;
as
a
single
and
a
promotional
track
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Michelob?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michelob"
class="mw-redirect">Michelob</a>
beer
brand,
which
had
also
marketed
earlier
songs
by
Collins
and
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Winwood">Steve
Winwood</a>.
Clapton
won
a
<a
href="/wiki/British_Academy_Television_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="British
Academy
Television
Award"
class="mw-redirect">British
Academy
Television
Award</a>
for
his
collaboration
with
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Kamen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Kamen">Michael
Kamen</a>
on
the
score
for
the
1985
<a
href="/wiki/BBC_Television?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC
Television">BBC
Television</a>
thriller
serial
<i><a
href="/wiki/Edge_of_Darkness?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Edge
of
Darkness">Edge
of
Darkness</a></i>.
In
1989,
Clapton
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Journeyman_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Journeyman
(album)">Journeyman</a></i>,
an
album
which
covered
a
wide
range
of
styles
including
blues,
jazz,
soul
and
pop.
Collaborators
included
George
Harrison,
Phil
Collins,
<a
href="/wiki/Daryl_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Daryl
Hall">Daryl
Hall</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Chaka_Khan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chaka
Khan">Chaka
Khan</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Mick_Jones_(Foreigner)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mick
Jones
(Foreigner)">Mick
Jones</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/David_Sanborn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Sanborn">David
Sanborn</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_Cray?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robert
Cray">Robert
Cray</a>.
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_BRIT_Awards_ceremonies?qsrc=3044#1987"
title="List
of
BRIT
Awards
ceremonies">1987</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Awards">Brit
Awards</a>
in
London,
Clapton
was
awarded
the
prize
for
Outstanding
Contribution
to
Music.<sup
id="cite_ref-Brits_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Brits-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Resurgence_and_stardom">Resurgence
and
stardom</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Resurgence
and
stardom">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>The
1990s
brought
a
series
of
32
concerts
to
the
Royal
Albert
Hall,
such
as
the
<a
href="/wiki/24_Nights?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="24
Nights">24
Nights</a>
series
of
concerts
that
took
place
around
January
through
February
1990,
and
February
to
March
1991.
On
<span
class="nowrap">27
August</span>
1990,
fellow
blues
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Stevie_Ray_Vaughan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stevie
Ray
Vaughan">Stevie
Ray
Vaughan</a>,
who
was
touring
with
Clapton,
and
three
members
of
their
road
crew
were
killed
in
a
helicopter
crash
between
concerts.
Then,
on
<span
class="nowrap">20
March</span>
1991,
Clapton's
four-year-old
son,
Conor,
died
after
falling
from
the
53rd-floor
window
of
his
mother's
friend's
New
York
City
apartment
at
117
East
57th
Street.
Conor's
funeral
took
place
on
28
March
at
St
Mary
Magdelene's
Church
in
Clapton's
home
village
in
<a
href="/wiki/Ripley,_Surrey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ripley,
Surrey">Ripley</a>,
Surrey.<sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton's
grief
was
expressed
in
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tears_in_Heaven?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tears
in
Heaven">Tears
in
Heaven</a>&quot;,
which
was
co-written
by
<a
href="/wiki/Will_Jennings?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Will
Jennings">Will
Jennings</a>.
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/35th_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="35th
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">35th
Grammy
Awards</a>,
Clapton
received
six
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>
for
the
single
&quot;Tears
in
Heaven&quot;
and
his
<i><a
href="/wiki/Unplugged_(Eric_Clapton_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unplugged
(Eric
Clapton
album)">Unplugged</a></i>
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
reached
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>,
and
has
since
been
certified
<a
href="/wiki/Diamond_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Diamond
album"
class="mw-redirect">Diamond</a>
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>
for
selling
over
10
million
copies
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
9
September
1992,
Clapton
performed
&quot;Tears
in
Heaven&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/1992_MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1992
MTV
Video
Music
Awards">1992
MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>
in
Los
Angeles,
and
won
the
award
for
Best
Male
Video.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
October
1992
Clapton
was
among
the
dozens
of
artists
performing
at
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Dylan">Bob
Dylan</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/30th_Anniversary_Concert_Celebration?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="30th
Anniversary
Concert
Celebration"
class="mw-redirect">30th
Anniversary
Concert
Celebration</a>.
Recorded
at
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>
in
New
York
City,
the
live
two-disk
CD/DVD
captured
a
show
full
of
celebrities
performing
classic
Dylan
songs,
before
ending
with
a
few
performances
from
Dylan
himself.
Despite
the
presence
of
10
other
guitarists
on
stage,
including
George
Harrison,
<a
href="/wiki/Neil_Young?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Neil
Young">Neil
Young</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_McGuinn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
McGuinn">Roger
McGuinn</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Cropper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Cropper">Steve
Cropper</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Petty?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Petty">Tom
Petty</a>,
and
Dylan,
Clapton
played
the
lead
on
a
nearly
7-minute
version
of
Dylan's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Knockin%27_on_Heaven%27s_Door?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Knockin'
on
Heaven's
Door">Knockin'
on
Heaven's
Door</a>&quot;
as
part
of
the
finale.</p>








<p>While
<i>Unplugged</i>
featured
Clapton
playing
<a
href="/wiki/Steel-string_guitar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steel-string
guitar"
class="mw-redirect">acoustic
guitar</a>,
his
1994
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/From_the_Cradle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="From
the
Cradle">From
the
Cradle</a></i>
contained
new
versions
of
old
<a
href="/wiki/Blues_standards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues
standards"
class="mw-redirect">blues
standards</a>,
highlighted
by
his
electric
guitar
playing.<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton's
1996
recording
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Wayne_Kirkpatrick?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wayne
Kirkpatrick">Wayne
Kirkpatrick</a>/<a
href="/wiki/Gordon_Kennedy_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gordon
Kennedy
(musician)">Gordon
Kennedy</a>/<a
href="/wiki/Tommy_Sims?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tommy
Sims">Tommy
Sims</a>
tune
&quot;Change
the
World&quot;
(featured
in
the
soundtrack
of
the
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Phenomenon_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phenomenon
(film)">Phenomenon</a></i>)
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Song
of
the
Year">Grammy
Award
for
Song
of
the
Year</a>
in
1997,
the
same
year
he
recorded
<i>Retail
Therapy</i>
(an
album
of
<a
href="/wiki/Electronic_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electronic
music">electronic
music</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/Simon_Climie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Simon
Climie">Simon
Climie</a>
under
the
pseudonym
<a
href="/wiki/X-sample?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="X-sample"
class="mw-redirect">TDF</a>).
The
following
year,
Clapton
released
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pilgrim_(Eric_Clapton_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pilgrim
(Eric
Clapton
album)">Pilgrim</a></i>,
the
first
record
featuring
new
material
for
almost
a
decade.<sup
id="cite_ref-amg_49-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-amg-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
finished
the
twentieth
century
with
collaborations
with
<a
href="/wiki/Carlos_Santana?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carlos
Santana">Carlos
Santana</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/B._B._King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B.
B.
King"
class="mw-redirect">B.
B.
King</a>.</p>








<p>In
1996
Clapton
had
a
relationship
with
singer/songwriter
<a
href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sheryl
Crow">Sheryl
Crow</a>.
They
remain
friends,
and
Clapton
appeared
as
a
guest
on
Crow's
Central
Park
Concert.
The
duo
performed
a
Cream
hit
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/White_Room?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="White
Room">White
Room</a>&quot;.
Later,
Clapton
and
Crow
performed
an
alternate
version
of
&quot;Tulsa
Time&quot;
with
other
guitar
legends
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Crossroads_Guitar_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crossroads
Guitar
Festival">Crossroads
Guitar
Festival</a>
in
June
2007.</p>








<p>In
1998
Clapton,
then
53,
met
22-year-old
administrative
assistant
Melia
McEnery
in
<a
href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbus,
Ohio">Columbus,
Ohio</a>,
at
a
party
given
for
him
after
a
performance.
He
quietly
dated
her
for
a
year,
and
went
public
with
the
relationship
in
1999.
They
married
on
<span
class="nowrap">1
January</span>
2002
at
St
Mary
Magdalene
church
in
Clapton's
birthplace,
<a
href="/wiki/Ripley,_Surrey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ripley,
Surrey">Ripley</a>.
As
of
2005
they
have
three
daughters,
Julie
Rose
(<span
class="nowrap">13
June</span>
2001),
Ella
May
(<span
class="nowrap">14
January</span>
2003),
and
Sophie
Belle
(<span
class="nowrap">1
February</span>
2005).</p>








<p>At
the
<a
href="/wiki/41st_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="41st
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">41st
Grammy
Awards</a>
on
24
February
1999,
Clapton
received
his
third
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Male
Pop
Vocal
Performance">Grammy
Award
for
Best
Male
Pop
Vocal
Performance</a>,
for
his
song
&quot;My
Father's
Eyes&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
October
1999,
the
compilation
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Clapton_Chronicles:_The_Best_of_Eric_Clapton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Clapton
Chronicles:
The
Best
of
Eric
Clapton">Clapton
Chronicles:
The
Best
of
Eric
Clapton</a></i>,
was
released,
which
contained
a
new
song,
&quot;Blue
Eyes
Blue&quot;,
that
also
appears
in
soundtrack
for
the
film,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Runaway_Bride_(1999_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Runaway
Bride
(1999
film)">Runaway
Bride</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-60"
class="reference"><a

<p>Following
the
release
of
the
2001
record
<i><a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reptile
(album)">Reptile</a></i>,
in
June
2002,
Clapton
performed
&quot;Layla&quot;
and
&quot;While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Party_at_the_Palace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Party
at
the
Palace">Party
at
the
Palace</a>
concert
in
the
grounds
of
<a
href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buckingham
Palace">Buckingham
Palace</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-61"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
29
November
2002,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Concert_for_George?qsrc=3044"

for
George">Concert
for
George</a>

at

<a

title="Royal
Albert
Hall">Royal
Albert
Hall</a>,
a
tribute
to
George
Harrison,
who
had
died
a
year
earlier
of
lung
cancer.<sup

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2002concert-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup>

was
a
performer
and
the
musical
director.
The
concert
featured
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney?qsrc=3044"

McCartney</a>,

title="Tom
Petty

Heartbreakers">Tom
Petty
and

Heartbreakers</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Ravi_Shankar?qsrc=3044"

<a

title="Gary
Brooker">Gary
Brooker</a>,
Billy

<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe

(singer)">Joe

and
<a

two
albums
of

of

<a

<p>On
22
January
2005,
Clapton
performed
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Tsunami_Relief_Cardiff?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tsunami
Relief
Cardiff">Tsunami
Relief
Concert</a>
held
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Millennium
Stadium">Millennium
Stadium</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Cardiff?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>,
in
aid
of
the
victims
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2004
Indian
Ocean
earthquake"
class="mw-redirect">2004
Indian
Ocean
earthquake</a>.
In
May
2005
Eric
Clapton,
Jack
Bruce,
and
Ginger
Baker
reunited
as
Cream
for
a
series
of
concerts
at
the
Royal
Albert
Hall
in
London.
Concert
recordings
were
released
on
CD
and
DVD.
Later,
Cream
performed
in
New
York
at
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Back_Home_(Eric_Clapton_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
Home
(Eric
Clapton
album)">Back
Home</a></i>,
Clapton's
first
album
of
new
original
material
in
nearly
five
years,
was
released
on
<a
href="/wiki/Reprise_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reprise
Records">Reprise
Records</a>
on
<span
class="nowrap">30
August</span>.
In
2006
he
invited
<a
href="/wiki/Derek_Trucks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Derek
Trucks">Derek
Trucks</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Doyle_Bramhall_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doyle
Bramhall
II">Doyle
Bramhall
II</a>
to
join
his
band
for
his
2006–2007
world
tour.
Trucks
is
the
third
member
of
the
Allman
Brothers
Band
to
tour
supporting
Clapton,
the
second
being
pianist/keyboardist
<a
href="/wiki/Chuck_Leavell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chuck
Leavell">Chuck
Leavell</a>,
who
appeared
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Unplugged">MTV
Unplugged</a></i>
album
and
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/24_Nights?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="24
Nights">24
Nights</a></i>
performances
at
the
Royal
Albert
Hall
theatre
of
London
in
1990
and
1991,
as
well
as
Clapton's
1992
U.S.
tour.<sup
id="cite_ref-Music_Legends_64-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Music_Legends-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On

performed
with

Waters</a>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Highclere_Castle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Highclere
Castle">Highclere
Castle</a>,
Hampshire,
in
support
of
the
Countryside
Alliance.<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
<span
class="nowrap">13
August</span>
2006,
Clapton
made
a
guest
appearance
at
the
Bob
Dylan
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbus,
Ohio">Columbus,
Ohio</a>,
playing
guitar
on
three
songs
in
<a
href="/wiki/Jimmie_Vaughan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmie
Vaughan">Jimmie
Vaughan</a>'s
opening
act.<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
collaboration
with
guitarist
J.
J.
Cale,
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Road_to_Escondido?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Road
to
Escondido">The
Road
to
Escondido</a></i>,
was
released
on
<span
class="nowrap">7
November</span>
2006,
featuring
Derek
Trucks
and
Billy
Preston.
The
14-track
CD
was
produced
and
recorded
by
the
duo
in
August
2005
in
California.
The
chemistry
between
Trucks
and
Clapton
convinced
him
to
invite
<a
href="/wiki/The_Derek_Trucks_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Derek
Trucks
Band">The
Derek
Trucks
Band</a>
to
open
for
Clapton's
set
at
his
2007
<a
href="/wiki/Crossroads_Guitar_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crossroads
Guitar
Festival">Crossroads
Guitar
Festival</a>.
Trucks
remained
on
set
afterward,
performed
with
Clapton's
band
throughout
his
performances,
and
later
embarked
on
a
world
tour
with
him.</p>








<p>The
rights
to
Clapton's
official
memoirs,
written
by
Christopher
Simon
Sykes
and
published
in
2007,
were
sold
at
the
2005
<a
href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Book_Fair?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frankfurt
Book
Fair">Frankfurt
Book
Fair</a>
for
<span
class="nowrap">US$4
million</span>.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
26
February
2008,
it
was
reported
that
<a
href="/wiki/North_Korean?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="North
Korean"
class="mw-redirect">North
Korean</a>
officials
had
invited
Clapton
to
play
a
concert
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Communist_state?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Communist
state">communist
state</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton's
management
received
the
invitation
and
passed
it
on
to
the
singer,
who
agreed
in
principle
and
suggested
it
take
place
sometime
in
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
Kristen
Foster,
a
spokesperson,
said,
&quot;Eric
Clapton
receives
numerous
offers
to
play
in
countries
around
the
world,&quot;
and
&quot;[t]here
is
no
agreement
whatsoever
for
him
to
play
in
North
Korea.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Eric

<p>In
2007
Clapton
learned
more
about
his
father,
a
Canadian
soldier
who
left
the
UK
after
the
war.
Although
Clapton's
grandparents
eventually
told
him
the
truth
about
his
parentage,
he
only
knew
that
his
father's
name
was
Edward
Fryer.
This
was
a
source
of
disquiet
for
Clapton,
as
witnessed
by
his
1998
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/My_Father%27s_Eyes_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
Father's
Eyes
(song)">My
Father's
Eyes</a>&quot;.
A
<a
href="/wiki/Montreal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Montreal">Montreal</a>
journalist
named
Michael
Woloschuk
researched
Canadian
Armed
Forces
service
records
and
tracked
down
members
of
Fryer's
family,
and
finally
pieced
together
the
story.
He
learned
that
Clapton's
father
was
Edward
Walter
Fryer,
born
<span
class="nowrap">21
March</span>
1920,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Montreal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Montreal">Montreal</a>
and
died
<span
class="nowrap">15
May
1985</span>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Newmarket,_Ontario?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Newmarket,
Ontario">Newmarket,
Ontario</a>.
Fryer
was
a
musician
(piano
and
saxophone)
and
a
lifelong
drifter
who
was
married
several
times,
had
several
children,
and
apparently
never
knew
that
he
was
the
father
of
Eric
Clapton.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
thanked
Woloschuk
in
an
encounter
at
Macdonald
Cartier
Airport,
in
Ottawa,
Ontario,
Canada.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
February
2008
Clapton
performed
with
his
long-time
friend
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Winwood">Steve
Winwood</a>
at
Madison
Square
Garden
and
guested
on
his
recorded
single,
&quot;Dirty
City&quot;,
on
Winwood's
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nine_Lives_(Steve_Winwood_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nine
Lives
(Steve
Winwood
album)">Nine
Lives</a></i>.
The
two
former
Blind
Faith
bandmates
met
again
for
a
series
of
14
concerts
throughout
the
United
States
in
June
2009.</p>








<p>Clapton's
2008

began
on
<span
class="nowrap">3

at

<a

and

headlined

for
<a

(previously

from
<a

and
<a

<p>In
March
2009,
the
Allman
Brothers
Band
(amongst
many
notable
guests)
celebrated
their
40th
year,
dedicating
their
string
of
concerts
to
the
late
Duane
Allman
on
their
annual
run
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Beacon_Theatre_(New_York_City)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beacon
Theatre
(New
York
City)">Beacon
Theatre</a>.
Eric
Clapton
was
one
of
the
performers,
with
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Butch_Trucks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butch
Trucks">Butch
Trucks</a>
remarking
that
the
performance
was
not
the
typical
Allman
Brothers
experience,
given
the
number
and
musical
styles
of
the
guests
who
were
invited
to
perform.
Songs
like
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_Memory_of_Elizabeth_Reed?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Memory
of
Elizabeth
Reed">In
Memory
of
Elizabeth
Reed</a>&quot;
were
punctuated
with
others,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Weight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Weight">The
Weight</a>&quot;,
with
<a
href="/wiki/Levon_Helm?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Levon
Helm">Levon
Helm</a>;
<a
href="/wiki/Johnny_Winter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Johnny
Winter">Johnny
Winter</a>
sitting
in
on
Hendrix's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Red_House_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Red
House
(song)">Red
House</a>&quot;;
and
&quot;Layla&quot;.
On
<span
class="nowrap">4
May</span>
2009
Clapton
appeared
as
a
featured
guest
at
the
Royal
Albert
Hall,
playing
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Further_on_Up_the_Road?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Further
on
Up
the
Road"
class="mw-redirect">Further
on
Up
the
Road</a>&quot;
with
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Bonamassa?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Bonamassa">Joe
Bonamassa</a>.</p>








<p>Clapton
was

to
be
one

at

<a

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"

<p>Clapton
performed
a
two-night
show
with
<a
href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jeff
Beck">Jeff
Beck</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena_(London)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
O2
Arena
(London)"
class="mw-redirect">London's
O2
Arena</a>
on
<span
class="nowrap">13–14
February</span>
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
two
former
Yardbirds
extended
their
2010
tour
with
stops
at
Madison
Square
Garden,<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>

<a
href="/wiki/Air_Canada_Centre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Air
Canada
Centre">Air
Canada
Centre</a>
in
Toronto,
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bell_Centre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bell
Centre">Bell
Centre</a>
in
Montreal.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
performed
a
series
of
concerts
in
11
cities
throughout
the
United
States
from
<span
class="nowrap">25
February</span>
to
<span
class="nowrap">13
March</span>
2010,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Daltrey">Roger
Daltrey</a>
as
opening
act.
His
third
European
tour
with
Steve
Winwood
began
on
<span
class="nowrap">18
May</span>
and
ended
<span
class="nowrap">13
June</span>,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Norris_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Norris
(musician)">Tom
Norris</a>
as
opening
act.
He
then
began
a
short
North
American
tour
lasting
from
<span
class="nowrap">26
June</span>
to
<span
class="nowrap">3
July</span>,
starting
with
his
third
Crossroads
Guitar
Festival
on
<span
class="nowrap">26
June</span>
at
<a
href="/wiki/Toyota_Park_(Bridgeview)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toyota
Park
(Bridgeview)"
class="mw-redirect">Toyota
Park</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Bridgeview,_Illinois?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bridgeview,
Illinois">Bridgeview,
Illinois</a>.
Clapton
released
a
new
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Clapton_(2010_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Clapton
(2010
album)">Clapton</a></i>,
on
<span
class="nowrap">27
September</span>
2010
in

United
Kingdom
and
28
September
2010
in
the
United
States.
On
<span
class="nowrap">17
November</span>
2010,
Clapton
performed
as
guest
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Trust?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Prince's
Trust"
class="mw-redirect">Prince's
Trust</a>
rock
gala
held
at
the
Royal

Hall,
supported

house

for

which
included
<a

<p>On

Clapton

<a

On

<a

<i>Champagne

<p>In
January
2013,
Surfdog
Records
announced
a
signed
deal
with
Eric
for
the
release
of
his
forthcoming
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Old_Sock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Old
Sock">Old
Sock</a></i>
on
12
March.
On
8

2013,
Eric
and
Hard
Rock
International
launched
the
limited-edition
Eric
Clapton
Artist
Spotlight
merchandise

benefiting
Crossroads
Centre
Antigua.<sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
toured
the
United
States
and
Europe
from
14
March
to
19
June
2013
to
celebrate
his
50
years
as
a
professional
musician.<sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
15
October
2013
Eric's
popular
<a
href="/wiki/Unplugged_(Eric_Clapton_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unplugged
(Eric
Clapton
album)">Unplugged</a>
album
and
concert
DVD
were
re-released,
titled
<i>Unplugged:
Expanded
&amp;
Remastered.</i>
The
album
includes
the
original
14
tracks,
remastered,
as
well
as
6
additional
tracks,
including
2
versions
of
<a
href="/wiki/My_Father%27s_Eyes_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
Father's
Eyes
(song)">My
Father's
Eyes</a>.
The
DVD
includes
a
restored
version
of
the
concert,
as
well
as
over
60
minutes
of
unseen
footage
from
the
rehearsal.</p>








<p>On
November
13
and
14,
2013
Clapton
headlined
the
final
two
evenings
of
the
&quot;Baloise
Sessions&quot;,
an
annual
indoor
music
festival
in
<a
href="/wiki/Basel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Basel">Basel</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Switzerland?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.
The
concerts
took
place
in
the
Event
Halle,
Messe
Basel
and
a
one
hour
broadcasting
from
this
performance
was
aired
on
Swiss
radio
SRF3
on
18
November
2013.
Clapton
scheduled
a
series
of
concerts
in
Asia,
the
United
States
and
Europe
from
February
18
to
June
28,
2014.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Influences">Influences</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
Influences">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Clapton
cites
<a
href="/wiki/Freddie_King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Freddie
King">Freddie
King</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/B.B._King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B.B.
King">B.B.
King</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Albert_King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Albert
King">Albert
King</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buddy
Guy">Buddy
Guy</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Hubert_Sumlin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hubert
Sumlin">Hubert
Sumlin</a>
as
guitar
playing
influences.
Clapton
stated
blues
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robert
Johnson
(musician)"
class="mw-redirect">Robert
Johnson</a>
to
be
his
single
most
important
influence.
In
2004
Clapton
released
CDs
and
DVDs
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Me_and_Mr._Johnson?qsrc=3044#Sessions_for_Robert_J"
title="Me
and
Mr.
Johnson">Sessions
for
Robert
Johnson</a></i>,
featuring
Clapton
covering
Robert
Johnson
songs
using
electric
and
acoustic
guitars.<sup
id="cite_ref-86"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Clapton
co-authored
with
others
the
book
<i>Discovering
Robert
Johnson</i>,
in
which
Clapton
said
Johnson
was<sup
id="cite_ref-87"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<blockquote>









<p>&quot;...the
most
important
blues
musician
who
ever
lived.
He
was
true,
absolutely,
to
his
own
vision,
and
as
deep
as
I
have
gotten
into
the
music
over
the
last
30
years,
I
have
never
found
anything
more
deeply
soulful
than
Robert
Johnson.
His
music
remains
the
most
powerful
cry
that
I
think
you
can
find
in
the
human
voice,
really.
...
it
seemed
to
echo
something
I
had
always
felt.&quot;</p>








</blockquote>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Legacy">Legacy</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14"
title="Edit
section:
Legacy">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Clapton
has
been
referred
to
as
one
of
the
most
important
and
influential
guitarists
of
all
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-AST_1-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AST-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Meisel_88-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Meisel-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-89"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-90"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
is
the
only
three-time
inductee
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>:
once
as
a
solo
artist,
and
separately
as
a
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Yardbirds">The
Yardbirds</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Cream_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cream
(band)">Cream</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rock_Hall_4-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rock_Hall-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
ranked
second
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone
(magazine)"
class="mw-redirect">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
magazine's
list
of
the
&quot;100
Greatest
Guitarists
of
All
Time&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-RS_2-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
fourth
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Gibson_Guitar_Corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
Guitar
Corporation">Gibson's</a></i>
Top
50
Guitarists
of
All
Time.<sup
id="cite_ref-Gibson_3-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Gibson-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Guitarists
influenced
by
Clapton
include

<span

tright">

Clapton
on
the
There's
One
in
Every
Crowd
Tour,
with
&quot;










<a
href="/wiki/Blackie_(guitar)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

(guitar)">Blackie</a>&quot;

<p>Clapton's
choice
of
electric
guitars
has
been
as
notable
as
the
man
himself;
alongside
<a
href="/wiki/Hank_Marvin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hank
Marvin">Hank
Marvin</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>
and
Jimi
Hendrix,
Clapton
exerted
a
crucial
and
widespread
influence
in
popularising
particular
models
of
electric
guitar.<sup
id="cite_ref-93"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
With
the
Yardbirds,
Clapton
played
a
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Telecaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Telecaster">Fender
Telecaster</a>,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Jazzmaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Jazzmaster">Fender
Jazzmaster</a>,
a
double-cutaway
<a
href="/wiki/Gretsch_6120?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gretsch
6120">Gretsch
6120</a>,
and
a
1964
Cherry-Red
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_Guitar_Corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
Guitar
Corporation">Gibson</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_ES-335?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
ES-335">ES-335</a>.
He
became
exclusively
a
Gibson
player
for
a
period
beginning
in
mid-1965,
when
he
purchased
a
used
sunburst
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
Les
Paul">Gibson
Les
Paul</a>
guitar
from
a
guitar
store
in
London.
Clapton
commented
on
the
slim
profile
of
the
neck,
which
would
indicate
it
was
a
1960
model.<sup
id="cite_ref-94"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Early
during
his
stint
in
Cream,
Clapton's
first
Les
Paul
Standard
was
stolen.
He
continued
to
play
Les
Pauls
exclusively
with
Cream
(one
bought
from
<a
href="/wiki/Andy_Summers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Andy
Summers">Andy
Summers</a>
was
almost
identical
to
the
stolen
guitar)<sup
id="cite_ref-95"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup>
until
1967,
when
he
acquired
his
most
famous
guitar
in
this
period,
a
1964
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_SG?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
SG">Gibson
SG</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-GIBS_96-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-GIBS-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
Just
before
Cream's
first
U.S.
appearance
in
1967,
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_SG?qsrc=3044#Unique_SGs"
title="Gibson
SG">Clapton's
SG</a>,
Bruce's
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_VI?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
VI"
class="mw-redirect">Fender
VI</a>,
and
Baker's
drum
head
were
all
repainted
in
psychedelic
designs
created
by
the
visual
art
collective
known
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Fool_(design_collective)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Fool
(design
collective)">The
Fool</a>.
In
1968
Clapton
bought
a
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_Firebird?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
Firebird">Gibson
Firebird</a>
and
started
using
the
1964
Cherry-Red
Gibson
ES-335
again.<sup
id="cite_ref-GIBS_96-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-GIBS-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
aforementioned
1964
ES-335
had
a
storied
career.
Clapton
used
it
at
the
last
Cream
show
in
November
1968
as
well
as
with
Blind
Faith,
played
it
sparingly
for
slide
pieces
in
the
1970s,
used
it
on
&quot;Hard
Times&quot;
from
<i><a
href="/wiki/Journeyman_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Journeyman
(album)">Journeyman</a></i>,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Live_in_Hyde_Park_(Eric_Clapton_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
in
Hyde
Park
(Eric
Clapton
album)">Hyde
Park</a>
live
concert
of
1996,
and
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/From_the_Cradle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="From
the
Cradle">From
the
Cradle</a></i>
sessions
and
tour
of
1994–95.
It
was
sold
for
US$847,500
at
a
2004
auction.<sup
id="cite_ref-cdqimo_97-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cdqimo-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup>
Gibson
produced
a
limited
run
of
250
&quot;Crossroads
335&quot;
replicas.
The
335
was
only
the
second
electric
guitar
Clapton
bought.<sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
July
1968
Clapton
gave
George
Harrison
a
1957
'goldtop'
Gibson
Les
Paul
that
been
refinished
with
a
red
colour.
The
following
September,
Clapton
played
the
guitar
on
the
Beatles'
studio
recording
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps">While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps</a>&quot;.
His
SG
found
its
way
into
the
hands
of
George
Harrison's
friend
<a
href="/wiki/Jackie_Lomax?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jackie
Lomax">Jackie
Lomax</a>,
who
subsequently
sold
it
to
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Todd_Rundgren?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Todd
Rundgren">Todd
Rundgren</a>
for
US$500
in
1972.
Rundgren
restored
the
guitar
and
nicknamed
it
&quot;Sunny&quot;,
after
&quot;Sunshine
of
Your
Love&quot;.
He
retained
it
until
2000,
when
he
sold
it
at
an
auction
for
US$150,000.<sup
id="cite_ref-GIBS_96-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-GIBS-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
1969
Blind
Faith
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyde
Park,
London">Hyde
Park,
London</a>
Clapton
played
a
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Musical_Instruments_Corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Musical
Instruments
Corporation">Fender</a>
Custom
<a
href="/wiki/Telecaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Telecaster"
class="mw-redirect">Telecaster</a>,
which
was
fitted
with
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Brownie_(guitar)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brownie
(guitar)">Brownie</a>&quot;<span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
neck.</p>








<p>In
late
1969
Clapton
made
the
switch
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Stratocaster">Fender
Stratocaster</a>.
&quot;I
had
a
lot
of
influences
when
I
took
up
the
Strat.
First
there
was
<a
href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buddy
Holly">Buddy
Holly</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buddy
Guy">Buddy
Guy</a>.
Hank
Marvin
was
the
first
well
known
person
over
here
in
England
who
was
using
one,
but
that
wasn't
really
my
kind
of
music.
Steve
Winwood
had
so
much
credibility,
and
when
he
started
playing
one,
I
thought,
oh,
if
he
can
do
it,
I
can
do
it.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first—used
during
the
recording
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Clapton
(album)">Eric
Clapton</a></i>—was
&quot;Brownie&quot;,
which
in
1974
became
the
backup
to
the
most
famous
of
all
Clapton's
guitars,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Blackie_(guitar)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blackie
(guitar)">Blackie</a>&quot;.
In
November
1970
Eric
bought
six
Fender
Stratocasters
from
the
Sho-bud
guitar
shop
in
<a
href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nashville,
Tennessee">Nashville,
Tennessee</a>
while
on
tour
with
the
Dominos.
He
gave
one
each
to
George
Harrison,
Steve
Winwood,
and
Pete
Townshend.</p>

<p>Clapton
assembled
the
best
components
of
the
remaining
three
to
create
&quot;Blackie&quot;,
which
was
his
favourite
stage
guitar
until
its
retirement
in
1985.
It
was
first
played
live
<span
class="nowrap">13
January</span>
1973
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton%27s_Rainbow_Concert?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Clapton's
Rainbow
Concert">Rainbow
Concert</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
called
the
1956/57
Strat
a
&quot;mongrel&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-101"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
<span
class="nowrap">24
June</span>
2004,
Clapton
sold
&quot;Blackie&quot;
at
<a
href="/wiki/Christie%27s?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christie's">Christie's</a>
Auction
House,
New
York,
for
US$959,500
to
raise
funds
for
his
<a
href="/wiki/Crossroads_Centre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crossroads
Centre">Crossroads
Centre</a>
for
drug
and
alcohol
addictions.
&quot;Brownie&quot;
is
now
on
display
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Experience_Music_Project?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Experience
Music
Project"
class="mw-redirect">Experience
Music
Project</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-102"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
<a
href="/wiki/Fender_Custom_Shop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fender
Custom
Shop">Fender
Custom
Shop</a>
has
since
produced
a
limited
run
of
275
'Blackie'
replicas,
correct
in
every
detail
right
down
to
the
'Duck
Brothers'
flight
case,
and
artificially
aged
using
Fender's
'Relic'
process
to
simulate
years
of
hard
wear.
One
was
presented
to
Eric
upon
the
model's
release
and
was
used
for
three
numbers
during
a
concert
at
the
Royal
Albert
Hall
on
<span
class="nowrap">17
May</span>
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-103"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1981
Clapton
gave
his
signed
Fender
Lead
II
guitar
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Cafe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
Rock
Cafe">Hard
Rock
Cafe</a>
to
designate
his
favourite
bar
stool.
Pete
Townshend
also
donated
his
own
Gibson
Les
Paul
guitar,
with
a
note
attached:
&quot;Mine's
as
good
as
his!
Love,
Pete.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-104"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1988
Fender
honoured
Clapton
with
the
introduction
of
his
signature
<a
href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_Stratocaster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Clapton
Stratocaster">Eric
Clapton
Stratocaster</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-jhfyzq_105-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-jhfyzq-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup>
This,
and
the
Yngwie
Malmsteen
Stratocaster,
were
the
first
two
artist
models
in
the
Stratocaster
range.
Since
then,
the
artist
series
has
grown
to
include
models
inspired
by
Clapton's
contemporaries
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Rory_Gallagher?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rory
Gallagher">Rory
Gallagher</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mark
Knopfler">Mark
Knopfler</a>,
Jeff
Beck,
and
Stevie
Ray
Vaughan,
and
by
those
who
have
influenced
him,
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buddy
Guy">Buddy
Guy</a>.
Clapton
uses
<a
href="/wiki/Ernie_Ball?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ernie
Ball">Ernie
Ball</a>
Slinky
and
Super
Slinky
strings,
gauge
.10
to.46.<sup
id="cite_ref-106"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
has
been
honoured
with
several
signature-model
000-sized
acoustic
guitars
made
by
the
American
firm
of
<a
href="/wiki/C.F._Martin_%26_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="C.F.
Martin
&amp;
Company"
class="mw-redirect">C.F.
Martin
&amp;
Company</a>.
The
first,
of
these,
introduced
in
1995,
was
a
limited
edition
000-42EC
Eric
Clapton
signature
model
with
a
production
run
of
461.
As
of
December
2007,
Martin
had
produced
seven
EC
signature
models.<sup
id="cite_ref-EC000_107-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-EC000-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
1939
000-42
Martin
that
he
played
on
the
<i>Unplugged</i>
album
sold
for
US$791,500
at
auction.<sup
id="cite_ref-cdqimo_97-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cdqimo-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup>
Clapton
plays
a
custom
000-ECHF
Martin
these
days.</p>








<p>In
1999,
Clapton
auctioned
off
some
of
his
guitar
collection
to
raise
more
than
US$5
million
for
continuing
support
of
the
Crossroads
Centre
in
Antigua,
which
he
founded
in
1997.<sup
id="cite_ref-108"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
Crossroads
Centre
is
a
treatment
base
for
addictive
disorders
such
as
drugs
and
alcohol.
In
2004
Clapton
organised
and
participated
in
the
Crossroads
Guitar
Festival
to
benefit
the
Centre.
A
second
guitar
auction,
including
the
&quot;Cream&quot;
of
Clapton's
collection
–
as
well
as
guitars
donated
by
famous
friends
–
was
held
on
<span
class="nowrap">24
June</span>
2004.
His
<a
href="/wiki/George_Lowden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Lowden">Lowden</a>
acoustic
guitar
sold
for
US$41,825.
The
revenue
garnered
by
this
auction
at
Christie's
was
US$7,438,624.<sup
id="cite_ref-cdqimo_97-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cdqimo-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2010
Eric
Clapton
announced
that
he
would
be
auctioning
off
over
150
items
at
a
New
York
auction
in
2011.
Proceeds
will
benefit
his
Crossroads
Centre
in
Antigua.
Items
include
Clapton's
guitar
from
the
Cream
reunion
tour
in
2005,
speaker
cabinets
used
in
the
early
1970s
from
his
days
with
Derek
and
the
Dominoes,
and
some
guitars
from
Jeff
Beck,
JJ
Cale,
and
Joe
Bonamassa.<sup
id="cite_ref-109"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
March
2011
Clapton
raised
more
than
US$2.15
million
when
he
auctioned
off
key
items,
including
a
1984
Gibson
<a
href="/wiki/Semi-acoustic_guitar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Semi-acoustic
guitar">hollow
body
guitar</a>,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Gianni_Versace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gianni
Versace">Gianni
Versace</a>
suit
from
his
1990
concert
at
the
Royal
Albert
Hall,
and
a
replica
of
the
famous
Fender
Stratocaster
known
as
&quot;Blackie&quot;,
which
fetched
more
than
$30,000.
All
proceeds
from
the
auction
were
donated
to
Clapton's
Crossroads
drug
and
rehabilitation
centre
in
Antigua.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Woman_tone">Woman
tone</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"
title="Edit
section:
Woman
tone">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>The
&quot;woman
tone&quot;
is
the
informal
term
used
by
Clapton
to
refer
to
his
distinctive
mid-
to
late-1960s
electric
guitar
sound,
created
using
his
<a
href="/wiki/Gibson_SG?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gibson
SG">Gibson
SG</a>
solid
body
guitar
(with
<a
href="/wiki/Humbucker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Humbucker">Humbucker</a>
pick-ups)
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplifiers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marshall
Amplifiers"
class="mw-redirect">Marshall</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Vacuum_tube?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vacuum
tube">tube</a>
amplifier.<sup
id="cite_ref-110"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
is
an
overdriven
sound
that
is
articulate
yet
thick.
It
is
characterised
by
being
quite
distorted
(or
even
achieved
with
a
fuzz)
but
muted,
in
contrast
to
the
bright
and
twangy
distortion
that
most
guitarists
were
using
at
the
time.</p>








<p>Among
the
techniques
used
to
replicate
Clapton's
sound
is
a
technique
by
which
the
amplifier's
volume
is
turned
up
to
full,
while
the
guitar's
tone
knob
is
turned
down
to
zero
or
one.<sup
id="cite_ref-111"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Perhaps
the
best
example
of
the
&quot;woman
tone&quot;
is
Clapton's
famous
riff
and
solo
from
Cream's
1967
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Sunshine_of_Your_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sunshine
of
Your
Love">Sunshine
of
Your
Love</a>&quot;.
Clapton
has
explained
that
he
obtained
the
tone
with
his
Gibson's
tone
control
rolled
all
the
way
down,
switching
the
neck
pick-up
(closest
to
the
fretboard)
and
the
volume
all
the
way
up,
with
his
distortion
turned
all
the
way
up.
The
treble,
mids
and
bass
controls
on
the
amplifier
were
also
maxed
out.
Some
versions
of
the
&quot;woman
tone&quot;
may
also
have
involved
strategic
positioning
of
Clapton's
<a
href="/wiki/Wah-wah_pedal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wah-wah
pedal">wah-wah
pedal</a>.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(September
2012)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Other_media_appearances">Other
media
appearances</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17"
title="Edit
section:
Other
media
appearances">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Clapton
frequently
appears
as
a
guest
on
the
albums
of
other
musicians.
For
example,
he
is
credited
on
<a
href="/wiki/Dire_Straits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dire
Straits">Dire
Straits</a><span

<i><a
href="/wiki/Brothers_in_Arms_(Dire_Straits_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brothers
in
Arms
(Dire
Straits
album)">Brothers
in
Arms</a></i>
album,
as
he
lent
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mark
Knopfler">Mark
Knopfler</a>
one
of
his
guitars.
He
played
lead
guitar
and
synthesiser
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Pros_and_Cons_of_Hitch_Hiking?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

Pros
and
Cons
of
Hitch
Hiking">The
Pros
and
Cons
of
Hitch
Hiking</a></i>,
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Waters?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Waters">Roger
Waters</a>'
debut
solo
album.
Other
media
appearances
include
the
<a
href="/wiki/Toots_%26_the_Maytals?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

&amp;
the
Maytals"

&amp;
the
Maytals</a>
album
<i><a

&amp;

&quot;<a

<p>Clapton
was

<a

Fender
cell

<p>Eric
Clapton
was
compared
to
God's
image
in
the

&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Holy_Crap!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

of

two

<i><a

'70s
Show</a></i>

characters
<a

by

minister
to

a

of

<p>Eric
Clapton
appeared
on
Top
Gear
in
2013,
during
Series
19
Episode
4
and
was
involved
in
testing
the
new
<a
href="/wiki/Kia_Cee%27d?qsrc=3044"

Cee'd</a>.

was

upon
to
test
the
Cee'd's
auxiliary
input,
which
he
tested
by
plugging
in
one
of

and

several

of

was

by

Clarkson
to
simply
be
